<div>

<p align="right" style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:right;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Exhibit 99.2</font></b></p>

<p align="right" style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:right;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;letter-spacing:-.15pt;">Independent Auditors&#146;
Report</font></b></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;letter-spacing:-.15pt;">To the Board of Directors</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;letter-spacing:-.15pt;">Implant Sciences Corporation:</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Wakefield, Massachusetts</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;letter-spacing:-.15pt;">We have audited the accompanying consolidated
balance sheets of Core Systems, Inc., (the &#147;Company&#148;), as of November 30, 2003
and September 30, 2004, and the related consolidated statements of operations,
stockholders&#146; deficit and cash flows for the twelve and ten month periods ended
November 30, 2003 and September 30, 2004 respectively.&#160; The consolidated financial statements are the
responsibility of the Company&#146;s management.&nbsp; Our responsibility is to
express an opinion on these financial statements based on our audits.</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;letter-spacing:-.15pt;">We conducted our audits in accordance with
auditing standards of the Public Company Accounting Oversight Board in the
United States of America.&#160; Those
standards require that we plan and perform the audits to obtain reasonable
assurance about whether the financial statements are free of material
misstatement.&nbsp; An audit includes examining, on a test basis, evidence
supporting the amounts and disclosures in the financial statements.&nbsp; An
audit also includes assessing the accounting principles used and significant
estimates made by management, as well as evaluating the overall financial
statement presentation.&nbsp; We believe that our audits provide a reasonable
basis for our opinion.</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;letter-spacing:-.15pt;">In our opinion, the consolidated financial
statements referred to above present fairly, in all material respects, the
financial position of Core Systems, Inc. as of November 30, 2003 and September 30,
2004 and the results of their operations and their cash flows for the twelve
and ten month periods then ended, respectively, in conformity with accounting
principles generally accepted in the United States of America.</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt 5.0in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">/s/ Nation Smith Hermes Diamond</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;letter-spacing:-.15pt;">San Diego, California</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;letter-spacing:-.15pt;">December 23, 2004</font></p>

<p align="center" style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">


<div style="font-family:Times New Roman;">

<p align="center" style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:-.25in;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">1.</font></b><b><font size="1" style="font-size:3.0pt;font-weight:bold;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font>Description of Business</b></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-indent:-.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Core Systems, Inc. (the &#147;Company&#148;), a California
corporation formed in 1990, provides ion implantation, disk refurbishment and
implant equipment upgrades to companies in the semiconductor industry.&#160; KryCore, Inc. a California corporation
wholly-owned by Core Systems, was formed in November 2001, and manufactures ion
source reconditioning systems to companies in the semiconductor industry.&#160; While the Company strives to offer quality
services and quick turnaround, it is subject to a number of risks similar to
other technology-based companies, including risks related to: (a) its
dependence on key individuals; and (b) competition from substitute products and
larger companies.</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">For the year ended November 30, 2003 and the
ten month period ended September 30, 2004, the Company reported a net loss of
$1,018,000 and $1,051,000 and used $172,000 and $176,000 in cash and cash
equivalents from operations, respectively.&#160;
As of November 30, 2003 and September 30, 2004, the Company had an
accumulated deficit of approximately $2,397,000 and $3,478,000,
respectively.&#160; Management continually
evaluates plans to reduce its operating expenses and increase its cash flow
from operations.&#160; Failure of the Company
to achieve its projections will require the Company to seek additional financing.&#160; There can be no guarantee that financing will
be available at commercially favorable terms.&#160;
The Company was acquired on October 15, 2004.&#160; See Note 12.</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:-.25in;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">2.</font></b><b><font size="1" style="font-size:3.0pt;font-weight:bold;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font>Summary of Significant Accounting
Policies</b></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-indent:-.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;"><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;">Cash and Cash Equivalents</font></i></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Company considers any securities with
maturities of 90 days or less at the time of investment to be cash equivalents.</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;"><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;">Financial Instruments</font></i></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The estimated fair values of the Company&#146;s
financial instruments, which at November 30, 2003 and September 30, 2004
include cash equivalents, accounts receivable, accounts payable, long-term
debt, convertible debt and Series A and Series B Preferred Stock, approximates
their carrying values due to their short-term nature or market variable rates
of interest.</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;"><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;">Inventories</font></i></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Inventories consist of raw materials and are
stated at the lower of cost (first in, first out) or market.</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;"><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;">Property and Equipment and Capital Leases</font></i></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Equipment and leasehold improvements are
stated at cost.&#160; Equipment is depreciated
using the straight-line method over the estimated useful lives of the assets,
ranging from five to twenty years.&#160;
Capitalized leases and leasehold improvements are amortized based upon
the lesser of the term of the lease or the useful life of the asset and such
expense is included in depreciation expense.&#160;
Expenditures for repairs and maintenance are charged to expense as
incurred.</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

  <p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">3 - 7 years</font></p>
  </td>
 </tr>
 <tr>
  <td width="55%" valign="top" style="padding:0in 0in 0in 0in;width:55.4%;">
  <p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Motor vehicles</font></p>
  </td>
  <td width="3%" valign="bottom" style="padding:0in 0in 0in 0in;width:3.26%;">
  <p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:1.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
  </td>
  <td width="41%" valign="top" style="padding:0in 0in 0in 0in;width:41.34%;">
  <p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-autospace:none;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">7 years</font></p>
  </td>

</table>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;"><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;">Warranty Costs</font></i></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Company accrues warranty costs in the
period the related revenue is recognized.&#160;
Warranty costs and related accruals</font></p>

<p align="center" style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="center" style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">6</font></p>

<div style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">

<hr size="2" width="100%" noshade color="gray" align="left">

</font></div>

<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">


<div>

<p align="center" style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">are not material to operating results.&#160;
There were no warranty costs in 2003 or 2004.</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;"><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;">Intangible Asset</font></i></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The intangible asset is being amortized over
five years using the straight-line method.</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;"><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;">Income Taxes</font></i></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The liability method is used to account for
income taxes.&#160; Deferred tax assets and
liabilities are determined based on differences between the financial reporting
and income tax bases of assets and liabilities as well as net operating loss
and tax credit carry forwards and are measured using the enacted tax rates and
laws that will be in effect when the differences reverse.&#160; Deferred tax assets may be reduced by a
valuation allowance to reflect the uncertainty associated with their ultimate
realization.</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;"><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;">Impairment of Long-Lived Assets</font></i></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">In accordance with SFAS No. 144, &#147;Accounting
for the Impairment or Disposal of Long-Lived Assets,&#148; the Company reviews the
carrying values of its long-lived assets for possible impairment whenever
events or changes in circumstances indicate that the carrying amounts of the
assets may not be recoverable.</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Company believes that the carrying value
of its long-lived assets is fully realizable at September 30, 2004.</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;"><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;">Concentration of Credit Risk and Major
Customers</font></i></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Company grants credit to its customers,
primarily large corporations in the semiconductor industry.&#160; The Company performs periodic credit
evaluations of customer financial conditions and generally does not require
collateral.&#160; Receivables are generally
due within thirty days.&#160; Credit losses
have historically been minimal, which is consistent with management&#146;s
expectations.&#160; Reserves are provided for
estimated amounts of accounts receivable which may not be collected.&#160; Financial instruments that potentially subject
the Company to concentration of credit risk consist of trade receivables.</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Company has two major customers with
revenues in excess of 10% of the Company&#146;s total revenues either for the year
ended November 30, 2003 or the ten month period ended September 30, 2004, that
accounted for the following annual revenue:</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<div>

<p align="center" style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;"><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;">Employee Stock-Based Compensation</font></i></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Company accounts for its employee stock
based compensation arrangements under the provisions of Accounting Principles
Board (APB) Opinion No. 25, &#147;Accounting for Stock Issued to Employees,&#148; rather
than the alternative fair value accounting method provided for under SFAS No.
123, &#147;Accounting for Stock-Based Compensation.&#148;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Company has elected to use the
disclosure-only provisions of SFAS No. 123 and SFAS No. 148, &#147;Accounting for
Stock-Based Compensation-Transition and Disclosure.&#148;&#160; Had compensation expense for stock option
grants to employees been determined based on the fair value method at the grant
dates for awards under the stock option plans consistent with the method
prescribed by SFAS No. 123, the Company&#146;s net loss would have increased to the pro
forma amounts indicated as follows:</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

option pricing model prescribed by SFAS No. 123.&#160; In addition, deferred compensation has been
recorded relating to the repricing of stock options and stock options issued
below fair market value.&#160; The assumptions
used during each of the twelve and ten month periods ended November 30, 2003
and September 30, 2004, were as follows:</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;"><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;">Revenue Recognition</font></i></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Company recognizes revenue when there is
persuasive evidence of an arrangement with the customer which states a fixed or
determinable price and terms, delivery of the product has occurred or the
service performed in accordance with the terms of the sale, and collectibility
of the sale is reasonably assured.&#160; The Company
provides for estimated returns.</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;"><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;">Research and Development Costs</font></i></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">All costs of research and development
activities are expensed as incurred.&#160; The
Company performs research and</font></p>

<p align="center" style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<div style="font-family:Times New Roman;">

<p align="center" style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">development for itself.</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;"><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;">Principles of Consolidation</font></i></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The consolidated financial statements include
Core Systems, Inc. and its wholly owned subsidiary, Kry Core, Inc.,
Inter-company balances and transactions have been eliminated in consolidation.</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;"><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;">Recent Accounting Pronouncements</font></i></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">In December 2003, the Securities and Exchange
Commission (&#147;SEC&#148;) published Staff Accounting Bulletin (&#147;SAB&#148;) No. 104, &#147;Revenue
Recognition.&#148;&#160; SAB No. 104 was effective
upon issuance.&#160; The adoption of SAB No.
104 did not have a material effect on the Company&#146;s financial position, results
of operations, or cash flows.</font></p>

<p style="color:black;font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-indent:.25in;"><font color="black" face="Times New Roman" style="color:windowtext;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;"><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;">Use of Estimates</font></i></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The preparation of these financial statements
in conformity with accounting principles generally accepted in the United
States of America, requires management to make estimates and assumptions that
affect the reported amounts of assets and liabilities and disclosure of
contingent assets and liabilities at the date of the financial statements and
the reported amounts of revenues and expenses during the reporting
periods.&#160; Some of the more significant
estimates include allowance for doubtful accounts, and inventory
valuation.&#160; Management&#146;s estimates are
based on the facts and circumstances available at the time estimates are made,
past historical experience, risk of loss, general economic conditions and
trends and management&#146;s assessments of the probable future outcome of these
matters.&#160; Consequently, actual results
could differ from such estimates.</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:-.25in;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">3.</font></b><b><font size="1" style="font-size:3.0pt;font-weight:bold;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font>Property and Equipment</b></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:-.25in;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">5.</font></b><b><font size="1" style="font-size:3.0pt;font-weight:bold;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font>Related Party Transactions</b></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">SFAS No. 57, &#147;Related Party Disclosures,&#148;
specifies the nature of information that should be disclosed in financial
statements regarding related party transactions.</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Company entered into a certain Promissory
Note with Don Lindsey, and certain Convertible Promissory Notes with Teknet
Inc., and Zephyr Technologies.&#160; Don
Lindsey is the president and principal shareholder of the Company.&#160; Teknet and Zephyr Technologies are
corporations wholly owned by Don Lindsey.&#160;
Amounts due to Don Lindsey, Teknet and Zephyr under these notes are
approximately $447,000 and $449,000&#160; and
accounts payable of $0 and $6,000 relating to travel expenses on November 30,
2003 and September 30, 2004, respectively. &#160;See Note 10.</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Company entered into a Promissory Note
with Steve Lindsey.&#160; Steve Lindsey is an
employee and Secretary of the Company and the brother of Don Lindsey, president
and principal shareholder of the Company.&#160;
Amount due under the note to Steve Lindsey is $12,000 and accounts
payable of $1,000 for miscellaneous office expenses as of September 30, 2004.&#160; See Note 10.</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Company entered into a Convertible Note
with Walter Wriggins.&#160; Walter Wriggins is
an employee of the Company.&#160; The amount due
to Walter Wriggins under the note is $132,000 and accounts payable of $9,000
and $10,000 for travel expenses on November 30, 2003 and September 30, 2004,
respectively.&#160; See Note 10.</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Company entered into certain Convertible
Notes with Roland Lampert and Sunnyvale Industrial, Inc.&#160; Mr. Lampert is the owner of Sunnyvale Industrial
and Sunnyvale Industrial is the landlord of the Company&#146;s principal place of
business.&#160; Amounts due to Mr. Lampert and
Sunnyvale Industrial are approximately $561,000 and $861,000 on November 30,
2003 and September 30, 2004, respectively.&#160;
Unpaid rent due to Sunnyvale Industrial is $156,000 and $465,000 at
November 30, 2003 and September 30, 2004, respectively. &#160;See Note 10.</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Company entered into a Promisory Note in
the amount of $60,000 and a Convertible Note in the amount of $50,000 with the Pauly
Family Trust.&#160; Both notes are outstanding
as of November 30, 2003 and September 30, 2004.&#160;
Sandra Pauly is on the board of directors of the company.&#160; See Note 10.</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:-.25in;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">6.</font></b><b><font size="1" style="font-size:3.0pt;font-weight:bold;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font>Commitments and Contingencies</b></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-indent:-.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Capital and Operating Leases</font></b></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Company has an operating lease for its
manufacturing, research and office space which expires on November 30,
2004.&#160; The Company is negotiating with
its landlord to extend the lease.&#160; Under
the terms of the lease, the Company is responsible for its proportionate share
of real estate taxes and operating expenses relating to this facility.&#160; Total rental expense, including maintenance
and real estate tax expenses, for the twelve month period ended November 30,
2003 and the ten month period ending September 30, 2004 was $694,000 and
$431,000, respectively.</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Included in property and equipment at November
30, 2003 and September 30, 2004 is equipment recorded under capital leases with
a net book value of $139,000 and $165,000, respectively.&#160; Depreciation expense for property and equipment
under capital lease was $43,000 and $36,000 for the twelve and ten month
periods ended November 30, 2003 and September 30, 2004, respectively.&#160; (See Note 10).</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Future minimum rental payments required under
capital leases and operating leases with noncancelable</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">(b)&#160;
Other</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">From time to time, the Company is subject to
various claims, legal proceedings and investigations covering a wide range of
matters that arise in the ordinary course of its business activities.&#160; Each of these matters is subject to various
uncertainties.&#160; On the basis of
information presently available, the Company is not currently aware of any
legal proceedings or claims that the Company believes are likely to have a
material effect on the Company&#146;s consolidated financial position or
consolidated results of operations.</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">A valuation allowance has been established for the
Company&#146;s net deferred tax assets as their use is dependent on the generation
of sufficient future taxable income, which cannot be predicted at this time.</font></p>

<p style="color:black;font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font color="black" face="Times New Roman" style="color:windowtext;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">At September 30, 2004, the Company has the following
unused net operating loss and tax credit carryforwards available to offset
federal and state taxable income, both of which expire at various times through
2024.</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Company&#146;s net operating loss carryforwards are
subject to review and possible adjustment by the Internal Revenue Service and the
State of California and are subject to certain annual limitations as a result
of to the acquisition of the Company by Implant.</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:-.25in;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">8.</font></b><b><font size="1" style="font-size:3.0pt;font-weight:bold;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font>Stockholders&#146;
Equity</b></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-indent:-.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">(a)&#160; Option Activity</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">In May 1999, the Company adopted the 1999
Stock Option Plan (the &#147;Plan&#148;).&#160; The Plan
provides for the grant of incentive stock options and nonqualified stock
options to employees and directors.&#160; The
exercise price of the options equals 100% of the fair market value on the date
of the grant.&#160; Options expire ten years
from the date of the option grant and vest ratably over a four-year period
commencing with the second year.&#160; A total
of 305,000 options were reserved for issuance under the Plan.&#160; As of September 30, 2004, there are no
options available for issuance under the Plan.</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">In June 2004, the Company&#146;s Board of
Directors approved the repricing of all outstanding options to $1.25 per
share.&#160; The Company recorded deferred
compensation related to the difference between the fair market value and the
exercise price of the options.&#160; These
amounts will be expensed over the related vesting period.</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The following table presents the activity of
the 1999 Stock Option Plans for the twelve and ten month periods ended November
30, 2003 and September 30, 2004:</font></p>

<p align="center" style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">In October, 2004, all outstanding options
were exercised in full.&#160; See Subsequent
Event Note 11.</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-indent:-.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">(b)</font><font size="1" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font>Convertible
Debt (See Note 11)</p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">In October 2002, the Company issued
convertible debt to purchase 58,000 shares of common stock at an exercise price
of $4.00.&#160; This debt is payable in full
in 24 months.&#160; The notes were issued at
an interest rate of 10%.&#160; The Company
carries the notes on its books net of a $13,000 discount to reflect what it
believes is the fair market rate of interest.&#160;&#160;&#160;
This discount is being amortized to interest expense over the life of
the loan.&#160;&#160; The Company has recorded
approximately $7,000 and $6,000 of the discount as interest expense during the
periods ended November 30, 3003 and September 30, 2004, respectively.</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">In November 2002, the Company issued
convertible debt to purchase 114,375 shares of common stock at an exercise price
of $4.00.&#160; This debt is payable in full
in 24 months.&#160; The notes were issued at
an interest rate of 10%.&#160; The Company
carries the notes on its books net of a $ 26,000 discount to reflect what it
believes is the fair market rate of interest.&#160;
This discount is being amortized to interest expense over the life of
the loan.&#160;&#160; The Company has recorded
approximately $13,000 and $11,000 of the discount as interest expense during
the periods ended November 30, 3003 and September 30, 2004, respectively.</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

of $4.00.&#160; This debt is payable in full
in 12 months.&#160; The note was issued at an
interest rate of 10%. The Company has recorded approximately $4,000 of the
discount as interest expense during the period ending September 30, 2004.</font></p>

price of $2.74.&#160; This debt is payable in

at an interest rate of 10%.&#160; The Company

the loan.&#160;&#160; The Company has recorded

ending September 30, 2004.</font></p>

issued 67,000 shares of Series A Preferred Stock on January 19, 2002 for an
aggregate purchase price of $400,000.&#160;
The Company issued 59,000 shares of Series B Preferred Stock on May 31,
2002 for an aggregate purchase price of $500,000.&#160; The preferred shares are entitled to a
dividend, have certain conversion rights and a liquidation preference.&#160; <br>
See Note 11.</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-indent:-.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Company has a 401(k) Profit Sharing Plan
(the &#147;Plan&#148;) in which employees who have met certain service and eligibility
requirements may participate.&#160; Each
eligible employee may elect to contribute to the Plan, and the Company may make
discretionary matching contributions.&#160; No
contributions were made during the twelve and ten month periods ended November
30, 2003 or September 30, 2004.</font></p>

<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">


<div>

<p align="center" style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:black;font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:-.25in;"><b><font size="2" color="black" face="Times New Roman" style="color:windowtext;font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">10.</font></b><b><font size="1" color="black" face="Times New Roman" style="color:windowtext;font-size:3.0pt;font-weight:bold;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font></b><b><font color="black" face="Times New Roman" style="color:windowtext;font-weight:bold;">Long-term Debt</font></b></p>

<p style="color:black;font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-indent:-.25in;"><font color="black" face="Times New Roman" style="color:windowtext;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:black;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;"><b><font size="2" color="black" face="Times New Roman" style="color:windowtext;font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Capital Leases</font></b></p>

<p style="color:black;font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;"><font color="black" face="Times New Roman" style="color:windowtext;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Company purchases various pieces of
equipment financed under long-term capital leases. On February 27, 2002 the
Company entered into a long-term capital lease with GE Capital for the purchase
of various pieces of capital equipment.&#160;
The lease calls for monthly payments of $5,716 for a period of 36 months
ending February 2005.&#160; The lease carries
an annual effective interest rate of 22%.&#160;
Principal amounts outstanding under the lease are $71,000 and $22,000 on
November 30, 2003 and September 30, 2004, respectively.</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">On March 28, 2002 the Company entered into a
long&#150;term capital lease with Balboa Capital for the purchase of various pieces
of capital equipment.&#160; The lease calls
for monthly payments of $2,102 for a period of 48 months ending March
2006.&#160; The lease carries an annual
effective interest rate of 19%.&#160;
Principal amounts outstanding under the lease are $44,000 and $29,000 on
November 30, 2003 and September 30, 2004, respectively.</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<h1 align="left" style="color:windowtext;font-style:italic;font-weight:bold;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;page-break-after:auto;text-align:left;"><b><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:normal;">Convertible
Promissory Notes</font></i></b></h1>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">On October 1, 2003 the Company entered into a
Convertible Promissory Note with Dick Lee Corp., the Company&#146;s former landlord,
in the amount of approximately $190,000. The note represents past due rent on
the Company&#146;s principal place of business under the former lease.&#160; The note carries annual interest of 10% and
is payable when declared due by the holder after of a period of not less than
twelve months.&#160; The note and unpaid interest
is convertible, at the option of the holder, into shares of Company common
stock at a conversion price of $4.00 per share subject to certain antidilution
adjustments. The note is secured by certain stock warrants of the Company and
guaranteed by Don Lindsey, the president and principal shareholder of the
Company.&#160; The principal amount
outstanding is approximately $183,000 and $149,000 on November 30, 2003 and
September 30, 2004 respectively.</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Company entered into a series of
Convertible Promissory Notes with Zephyr Technologies. Zephyr Technologies is
wholly owned by Don Lindsey, the president and principal shareholder of the
Company.&#160; The notes carry an annual
interest of 10% and are payable when declared due and payable by the holders
after a period of not less than twenty-four months.&#160; The note and unpaid interest is convertible,
at the option of the holder, into shares of Company common stock at a
conversion price of $4.00 per share subject to certain antidilution
adjustments.&#160; The effective dates of the
notes are from November 2002 to June 2003.&#160;
The principal amount outstanding under the note is $400,000 on both November
30, 2003 and September 30, 2004.&#160; No
interest or principal has been paid or converted as of November 30, 2003 or
September 30, 2004.</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Company entered into a series of
Convertible Promissory Notes with various lenders. The notes carry an annual
interest of 10% and are payable when declared due and payable by the holders
after a period of not less than twenty-four months.&#160; The notes and unpaid interest are convertible,
at the option of the holders, into shares of Company common stock at a
conversion price of $4.00 per share subject to certain antidilution
adjustments.&#160; The effective dates of the
notes are from November 2002 and June 2003.&#160;
The principal amounts outstanding under the notes are approximately
$743,000 and $1,043,000 on November 30, 2003 and September 30, 2004
respectively.&#160; No interest or principal
have been paid or converted as of November 30, 2003 or September 30, 2004.</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:black;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;"><b><font size="2" color="black" face="Times New Roman" style="color:windowtext;font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Equipment Notes</font></b></p>

<p style="color:black;font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;"><font color="black" face="Times New Roman" style="color:windowtext;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Company entered into a series of notes
with a bank.&#160; The notes are used to
finance the purchase various pieces of capital equipment.&#160; The notes carry annual interest of 5.75% to
7.63% and maturities of from twelve months to sixty months.&#160; The notes are payable in monthly installments
of principal and interest until fully paid.&#160;
The effective dates of the notes are from August 1, 1999 to March 1,
2004 with maturities of December 2003 to December 2005. The principal amounts
of the notes outstanding are approximately $588,000 and $205,000 as of November
30, 2003 and September 30, 2004 respectively.</font></p>

<p align="center" style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<div>

<p align="center" style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:black;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;"><b><font size="2" color="black" face="Times New Roman" style="color:windowtext;font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Other Notes</font></b></p>

<p style="color:black;font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;"><font color="black" face="Times New Roman" style="color:windowtext;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Company entered into a Promissory Note with
Zephyr Technologies, an entity wholly owned by the president and principal
shareholder of the Company.&#160; The
effective date of the note is December 5, 2002.&#160;&#160; The note calls for principal not to exceed
$100,000 at an interest rate of prime plus 3%.&#160;
The initial amount of the note was $75,246.&#160; The note calls for monthly payments of $3,000
beginning January 6, 2003 and continuing until paid in full.&#160; The maturity date is January 6, 2004.&#160; During the course of the note the Company
failed to make monthly payments as provided by the note and the lender provided
additional funds to the Company under the note with the principal and interest
outstanding reaching $116,940.&#160; Effective
June 15, 2003 the lender and Company agreed to convert $100,000 of the note
balance to a Note convertible into Company common stock.&#160; The Company failed to pay the remaining
outstanding balance of the note on the maturity date as called for in the
note.&#160; The lender allowed the Company to
continue the note without penalty.&#160; The
principal amount of the note outstanding was approximately $12,000 and $14,000
on November 30, 2003 and September 30, 2004 respectively.</font></p>

<p style="color:black;font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-indent:.25in;"><font color="black" face="Times New Roman" style="color:windowtext;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Company entered into a Promissory Note with
Teknet, Inc., an entity wholly owned by the president and principal shareholder
of the Company, for $50,000.&#160; The
effective date of the note is December 1, 2001 with a maturity date of December
1, 2005.&#160; The principal amount of the
note outstanding is approximately $34,000 at November 30, 2003 and September
30, 2004.&#160; The note was settled for
approximately $24,000 in correlation with the Subsequent Event in Note 11.</font></p>

<p style="color:black;font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-indent:.25in;"><font color="black" face="Times New Roman" style="color:windowtext;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Company entered into a Promissory Note with Don
Lindsey, president and principal shareholder of the Company.&#160; The effective date of the note was September
20, 2002 in an initial amount of $27,000 at a rate of interest of 6% per annum.
The note calls for monthly payments of principal and interest beginning
December 1, 2002 and continuing until paid in full.&#160; The principal amount of the note may be
increased from time to time upon agreement by both parties. The principal
amount of the note outstanding was approximately $4,000 and $0 on November 30,
2003 and September 30, 2004 respectively.</font></p>

<p style="color:black;font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-indent:.25in;"><font color="black" face="Times New Roman" style="color:windowtext;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Company entered into a Promissory Note with
Steve Lindsey, an employee of the Company and brother of the president and
principal shareholder of the Company, for $12,000.&#160; The effective date of the note is January 21,
2004. The note calls for interest on the unpaid balance at a rate of 6% per
annum and monthly payments of principal and interest beginning February 21,
2004 and continuing until paid in full.&#160;
No monthly payments were made as called for under terms of the
note.&#160; The principal amount of the note
outstanding was $0 and $12,000 on November 30, 2003 and September 30, 2004
respectively.</font></p>

<p style="color:black;font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-indent:.25in;"><font color="black" face="Times New Roman" style="color:windowtext;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">On September 1, 1999 the Company entered into a
non-compete agreement with Don Weeks.&#160; Under
the terms of the non-compete Mr. Weeks agreed not to compete with the Company
in specific business involving ion implantation for a period of five years in
exchange for a payment of $200,000.&#160; The
payment was evidenced by a note for $200,000 payable in equal monthly
installments of $3,333 for a period of sixty months.&#160; The principal amount of the note outstanding
was $30,000 and $0 on November 30, 2003 and September 30, 2004 respectively.</font></p>

<p style="color:black;font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-indent:.25in;"><font color="black" face="Times New Roman" style="color:windowtext;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">On August 30, 1999 the Company entered into an
Agreement For The Purchase of Business Assets with IICO Corporation, a
corporation whose principal shareholders are Don Weeks and Diane Weeks.&#160; The Agreement called for payment of approximately
$96,000 with an initial payment of $13,000 and a Promissory Note with IICO Corporation
in the amount of approximately $83,000 for the purchase of certain tangible and
non-tangible assets of IICO Corporation.&#160;
Terms of the note call for equal monthly payments of $1,667 for a period
of sixty months beginning with September 1, 1999.&#160; The effective annual rate of interest on the
outstanding balance is 8%. The note is secured by certain assets of the
Company.&#160;&#160; The principal amount of the
note outstanding was approximately $18,000 and $0 on November 30, 2003 and
September 30, 2004 respectively.</font></p>

<p style="color:black;font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-indent:.25in;"><font color="black" face="Times New Roman" style="color:windowtext;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">On September 1, 2002 the Company entered into a
Factor Agreement with the Pauly Family Trust.&#160;
The agreement calls for the funding of $60,000 secured in general by the
full faith and credit of the Company and specifically by the Company Accounts
Receivable.&#160; The agreement calls for the
monthly payment of interest at an annual rate of 15% with a maturity at nine
months following the date of funding.&#160;
The Company failed to make monthly interest as required by the agreement
and failed to repay the principal at maturity.&#160;
The principal amount of the note outstanding was $60,000 and $60,000 on
November 30, 2003 and September 30, 2004 respectively.</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:black;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;"><b><font size="2" color="black" face="Times New Roman" style="color:windowtext;font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Lines of Credit</font></b></p>

<p style="color:black;font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;"><font color="black" face="Times New Roman" style="color:windowtext;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Company entered into a $1,000,000 Factoring Line
of Credit at an interest rate of prime plus 2.5% with its principal bank in
September 2003.&#160; The Factoring agreement
calls for the bank to advance 80% of qualified sales invoices to the Company in
exchange for a fee of 1% of each invoice advanced and interest.&#160; The agreement contains covenants which must
be reported monthly to the bank.&#160; As of
September 30, 2004, the Company was in violation of the net profit covenant;
however, in a letter dated December 29, 2004 the bank issued a waiver of this
default.&#160; The amount of the advances
outstanding was approximately $0 and $366,000 on November 30, 2003 and
September 30, 2004, respectively.</font></p>

<p style="color:black;font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-indent:.25in;"><font color="black" face="Times New Roman" style="color:windowtext;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman"><font style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Company had entered into an agreement for a Line
of Credit with its previous principal bank on April 1, 1996.&#160; The term of the agreement was 84 months at a
variable interest rate of 3.4 percentage points over the index.&#160;&#160; On February 23, 2004 the Company and the
bank agreed to terminate their relationship.&#160;
The Company paid down the outstanding Line of </font>Credit</font> by $300,000 with funds provided by their
current primary lender and agreed to pay the balance in monthly installments of
approximately $500, amortized over 120</p>

<p align="center" style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="center" style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">17</font></p>

<div style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">

<hr size="2" width="100%" noshade color="gray" align="left">

</font></div>

<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">


<div style="font-family:Times New Roman;">

<p align="center" style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:black;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;"><font size="2" color="black" face="Times New Roman" style="color:windowtext;font-size:10.0pt;">months, at an annual interest rate of 10%, with the balance
due in February, 2005.</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:-.25in;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">11.</font></b><b><font size="1" style="font-size:3.0pt;font-weight:bold;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font>Preferred
Stock</b></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Series A convertible preferred stock.</font></b></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">On January 18, 2002 the Company completed a private placement of 67,000
shares of Series A Preferred Stock for an aggregate purchase price of $400,000
and entered into an agreement with the Series A Preferred Stockholders. </font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The holders of the Series A Preferred Stock are entitled to receive
dividends in preference to any dividend on the common stock at the rate of 7%
per annum, when and as declared by the Company&#146;s board of directors.&#160; </font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Each holder of Preferred Stock shall have full voting rights and powers
equal to the voting rights and powers of the holders of Common Stock.&#160; The number of votes shall equal the number of
whole shares of Common Stock into which such shares of Preferred Stock could be
converted.</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The holders of the Series A Preferred Stock have the right to convert
the Series A Preferred Stock, at any time into common stock, with an initial
conversion rate of one-for-one.&#160; The
Company has reserved the shares of common stock to provide for the issuance
upon conversion of the Series A Preferred Stock.&#160; The Series A Preferred Stock shall automatically
convert into common stock (A) immediately prior to the closing of a firm
commitment underwritten public offering covering the offer and sale of Common
Stock in which the aggregate public offering price equals or exceeds
$15,000,000 and the public offering price per share equals or exceeds $17.91
per share, (B) immediately prior to a liquidation event in which the total
amount to be distributed exceeds $15,000,000, or (C) upon the Company&#146;s receipt
of the written consent of holders of at least two-thirds (2/3) of the then
outstanding shares of Preferred Stock to the conversion of all outstanding
Preferred Stock.</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Series A Preferred Stock is redeemable at any time commencing on
January 1, 2006 upon the written request of the holders of not less than a majority
of the outstanding shares of each Series A Preferred.&#160; The redemption price per share of each Series
A Preferred Stock shall be equal to the original purchase price (as adjusted
for any stock dividends, combinations or splits with respect to such shares).
Plus any accumulated or declared, but unpaid dividends.</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Series B convertible preferred stock</font></b></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">On May 31, 2002 the Company completed the private placement of 59,000
shares of Series B Preferred Stock for an aggregate purchase price of $500,000
and entered into an agreement with the Series B Preferred Stockholders.</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Each holder of
Preferred Stock shall have full voting rights and powers equal to the voting
rights and powers of the holders of Common Stock.&#160; The number of votes shall equal the number of
whole shares of Common Stock into which such shares of Preferred Stock could be
converted.</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The holders of the Series B Preferred Stock have the right to convert
the Series B Preferred Stock, at any time into common stock, with an initial
conversion rate of one-for-one.&#160; The
Company has reserved the shares of common stock to provide for the issuance
upon conversion of the Series B Preferred Stock.&#160; The Series B Preferred Stock shall
automatically convert into common stock (A) immediately prior to the closing of
a firm commitment underwritten public offering covering the offer and sale of
Common Stock in which the aggregate public offering price equals or exceeds
$15,000,000 and the public offering price per share equals or exceeds $17.91
per share, (B) immediately prior to a liquidation event in which the total
amount to be distributed exceeds $15,000,000, or (C) upon the Company&#146;s receipt
of the written consent of holders of at least two-thirds (2/3) of the then
outstanding shares of Preferred Stock to the conversion of all outstanding
Preferred Stock.</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Series B Preferred Stock is redeemable at any time commencing on
January 1, 2006 upon the written request of the holders of not less than a
majority of the outstanding shares of each Series B Preferred.&#160; The redemption price per share of each Series
B Preferred Stock shall be equal to the original purchase price (as adjusted
for any stock dividends, combinations or splits with respect to such shares).
Plus any accumulated or declared, but unpaid dividends.</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:black;font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:-.25in;"><b><font size="2" color="black" face="Times New Roman" style="color:windowtext;font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">12.</font></b><b><font size="1" color="black" face="Times New Roman" style="color:windowtext;font-size:3.0pt;font-weight:bold;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font></b><b><font color="black" face="Times New Roman" style="color:windowtext;font-weight:bold;">Subsequent
Events</font></b></p>

<p style="color:black;font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-indent:-.25in;"><font color="black" face="Times New Roman" style="color:windowtext;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">On October 13, 2004, Implant Sciences
Corporation (&#147;Implant&#148;) entered into a definitive agreement (the &#147;Merger Agreement&#148;) to acquire all of
the capital stock of the Company.&#160; The
transaction is being structured as a reorganization of Core with and into a
newly formed, wholly-owned subsidiary (&#147;Merger Sub&#148;) of Implant (the &#147;Transaction&#148;). As part of the
Transaction, Implant will issue to the former stockholders of the Company
consideration consisting of shares of Implant&#146;s common stock, par value $0.10
per share (&#147;Common Stock&#148;) equal in value to $3,250,000 (&#147;Stock Consideration&#148;),
and $2,000,000 in cash (&#147;Cash Consideration&#148;).&#160;
October 15, 2004 (&#147;Closing Date&#148;), Implant completed the acquisition of
the Company.&#160; In connection with the
Transaction, Implant issued 311,437 shares of its Common Stock as the Stock
Consideration and $2,000,000 in cash, to the Company Stockholders.</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The holders of the shares of Common Stock
comprising the Stock Consideration have agreed not to sell any of their shares
of Common Stock for a period six (6) months from the Closing Date (&#147;Lock-Up
Period&#148;).&#160; Pursuant to the terms of the
Merger Agreement, the shares of Common Stock comprising the Stock Consideration
will be adjusted in the event Implant&#146;s stock price at the end of the Lock-Up
Period is either greater than twenty-five percent (25%) higher or lower than
$10.4355 per share.&#160; In addition, the
Merger Agreement includes an Earnout provision equal to the Company&#146;s earnings
before taxes, depreciation and amortization for the twelve (12) month period
beginning on October 13, 2004 (the &#147;Earnout&#148;), the execution date of the Merger
Agreement, and ending on October 12, 2005 (&#147;Earnout Period&#148;), which will be
paid in the form of additional shares of Implant&#146;s Common Stock. The number of
shares to be issued in connection with the Earnout (the &#147;Earnout Shares&#148;), if
any, will be calculated by dividing the dollar amount of the Earnout by the
twenty (20) day average closing price of Implant&#146;s Common Stock prior to the
end of the Earnout Period (the &#147;Earnout Share Price&#148;).&#160; The Earnout Shares will also be subject to a
six (6) month lock-up, beginning on October 13, 2005, and will be adjusted in
the event Implant&#146;s stock price is either greater than twenty-five percent (25%)
higher or lower than the Earnout Share Price at the end of the Earnout lock-up
period.&#160; Implant has agreed to use its &#147;best-efforts&#148;
to file a registration statement with the Securities and Exchange Commission,
registering the resale of all of the shares of Common Stock included in the
Stock Consideration within six (6) months from the Closing Date.</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Additionally, pursuant to the terms of the
Merger Agreement, ten percent (10%) of each of the Stock Consideration and the
Cash Consideration has been heldback by Implant, pursuant to a holdback
agreement (&#147;Holdback Agreement&#148;), for a period of twelve (12) months from the
Closing Date (&#147;Holdback Period&#148;) for the purpose of settling any undisclosed
liabilities that may be discovered by Implant during the Holdback Period, for
indemnification of any breach of the representations and warranties made by the
Company and its primary stockholder in the Merger Agreement, and for other
potential expenses related to the Transaction.</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .25in;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">As part of the closing, Donald W. Lindsey,
the founder and CEO of the Company, has entered into a consulting agreement
with the Merger Sub for a period of one year beginning on the Closing Date,
whereby he will be required to perform technical and related consulting
services with respect to the Merger Sub&#146;s business.&#160; Walt Wriggins, the Company&#146;s Vice President
of Business Development/Operations has entered into a one-year employment
agreement with Implant&#146;s wholly-owned Merger Sub and has been named Vice
President of Business Development/Operations of the Merger Sub.</font></p>

<p align="center" style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-align:center;text-indent:.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="center" style="color:windowtext;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">18</font></p>

</font></div>
